	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Psychiatry</h1>
	
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
		<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
		<div id="contentSub"><span class="mw-redirectedfrom">&#160;&#160;(Redirected from <a href="/w/index.php?title=Psychiatric&amp;redirect=no" class="mw-redirect" title="Psychiatric">Psychiatric</a>)</span></div>
		
		
		
		<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>
		<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Not to be confused with <a href="/wiki/Clinical_psychology" title="Clinical psychology">Clinical psychology</a>.</div>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em"><caption>Psychiatry</caption><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center">Occupation</th></tr><tr><th scope="row">Names</th><td><a href="/wiki/Physician" title="Physician">Physician</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><div style="padding:0.1em 0;line-height:1.2em;">Activity sectors</div></th><td><a href="/wiki/Medicine" title="Medicine">Medicine</a></td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center">Description</th></tr><tr><th scope="row"><div style="padding:0.1em 0;line-height:1.2em;">Education required</div></th><td>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Doctor_of_Medicine" title="Doctor of Medicine">Doctor of Medicine</a> (MD) or</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Doctor_of_Osteopathic_Medicine" title="Doctor of Osteopathic Medicine">Doctor of Osteopathic Medicine</a> (DO) or</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bachelor_of_Medicine,_Bachelor_of_Surgery" title="Bachelor of Medicine, Bachelor of Surgery">Bachelor of Medicine, Bachelor of Surgery</a> (MBBS/MBChB)</li>
<li>plus a qualification in psychiatry</li></ul>
</td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><div style="padding:0.1em 0;line-height:1.2em;">Related jobs</div></th><td>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Specialty_(medicine)" title="Specialty (medicine)">Medical specialties</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Medicine" title="Medicine">Medicine</a></li></ul>
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Psychiatry</b> is the <a href="/wiki/Specialty_(medicine)" title="Specialty (medicine)">medical specialty</a> devoted to diagnosing, preventing, and treating <a href="/wiki/Mental_disorder" title="Mental disorder">mental disorders</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> These include various <a href="/wiki/Maladaptation" title="Maladaptation">maladaptations</a> related to mood, behavior, <a href="/wiki/Cognition" title="Cognition">cognition</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Perceptions" class="mw-redirect" title="Perceptions">perceptions</a>. See <a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_psychiatry" title="Glossary of psychiatry">glossary of psychiatry</a>.
</p><p>Psychiatric assessment of a person typically begins with a <a href="/wiki/Medical_history" title="Medical history">case history</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mental_status_examination" title="Mental status examination">mental status examination</a>. Physical examinations and <a href="/wiki/Psychological_testing" title="Psychological testing">psychological tests</a> may be conducted. <a href="/wiki/Neuroimaging" title="Neuroimaging">Neuroimaging</a> or other <a href="/wiki/Neurophysiology" title="Neurophysiology">neurophysiological</a> techniques may also be used.<sup id="cite_ref-NIMHSite_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NIMHSite-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> Mental disorders are often diagnosed under clinical concepts listed in diagnostic manuals. The <i><a href="/wiki/International_Statistical_Classification_of_Diseases_and_Related_Health_Problems" title="International Statistical Classification of Diseases and Related Health Problems">International Statistical Classification of Diseases and Related Health Problems</a></i> (ICD) is edited and used by the <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a> (WHO). The widely used <i><a href="/wiki/Diagnostic_and_Statistical_Manual_of_Mental_Disorders" title="Diagnostic and Statistical Manual of Mental Disorders">Diagnostic and Statistical Manual of Mental Disorders</a></i> (DSM) is published by the <a href="/wiki/American_Psychiatric_Association" title="American Psychiatric Association">American Psychiatric Association</a> (APA). The fifth edition of the DSM (<a href="/wiki/DSM-5" title="DSM-5">DSM-5</a>) was published in 2013. It included more up-to-date research<sup id="cite_ref-Kupfer_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kupfer-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> and re-organized the larger categories of various diseases.
</p><p>Nowadays, psychiatric treatment usually involves a combination of <a href="/wiki/Psychiatric_medication" title="Psychiatric medication">psychiatric medication</a> and <a href="/wiki/Psychotherapy" title="Psychotherapy">psychotherapy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> Modern practice also includes a wide variety of other modalities. These include <a href="/wiki/Assertive_community_treatment" title="Assertive community treatment">assertive community treatment</a>, <a href="/wiki/Community_reinforcement_approach_and_family_training" title="Community reinforcement approach and family training">community reinforcement</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Supported_employment" title="Supported employment">supported employment</a>. Treatment depends on the severity of functional impairment or other aspects of the disorder. It may be delivered on an <a href="/wiki/Inpatient" class="mw-redirect" title="Inpatient">inpatient</a> or <a href="/wiki/Outpatient" class="mw-redirect" title="Outpatient">outpatient</a> basis. An inpatient may be treated in a <a href="/wiki/Psychiatric_hospital" title="Psychiatric hospital">psychiatric hospital</a>. Research and treatment within psychiatry as a whole are conducted on an interdisciplinary basis (e.g., with <a href="/wiki/Epidemiologists" class="mw-redirect" title="Epidemiologists">epidemiologists</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mental_health_counselor" title="Mental health counselor">mental health counselors</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nursing" title="Nursing">nurses</a>, <a href="/wiki/Psychologists" class="mw-redirect" title="Psychologists">psychologists</a>, public health specialists, <a href="/wiki/Radiology" title="Radiology">radiologists</a> or <a href="/wiki/Social_workers" class="mw-redirect" title="Social workers">social workers</a>).
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Psychiatry&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:American_Lady_Against_The_Sky.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/American_Lady_Against_The_Sky.jpg/220px-American_Lady_Against_The_Sky.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/American_Lady_Against_The_Sky.jpg/330px-American_Lady_Against_The_Sky.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/American_Lady_Against_The_Sky.jpg/440px-American_Lady_Against_The_Sky.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3008" data-file-height="2000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:American_Lady_Against_The_Sky.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The word <i><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/psyche" class="extiw" title="wiktionary:psyche">psyche</a></i> comes from the <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greek" title="Ancient Greek">ancient Greek</a> for <a href="/wiki/Soul" title="Soul">soul</a> or <a href="/wiki/Butterfly" title="Butterfly">butterfly</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> The fluttering insect appears in the <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms" title="Coat of arms">coat of arms</a> of Britain's <a href="/wiki/Royal_College_of_Psychiatrists" title="Royal College of Psychiatrists">Royal College of Psychiatrists</a><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>The term "psychiatry" was first coined by the German <a href="/wiki/Physician" title="Physician">physician</a> <a href="/wiki/Johann_Christian_Reil" title="Johann Christian Reil">Johann Christian Reil</a> in 1808 and literally means the 'medical treatment of the soul' (<i><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/psych" class="extiw" title="wikt:psych">psych-</a></i> "soul" from <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greek" title="Ancient Greek">Ancient Greek</a> <i>psykhē</i> "soul"; <i><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/-iatry" class="extiw" title="wikt:-iatry">-iatry</a></i> "medical treatment" from Gk. <i>iātrikos</i> "medical" from <i>iāsthai</i> "to heal"). A medical doctor specializing in psychiatry is a <a href="/wiki/Psychiatrist" title="Psychiatrist">psychiatrist</a>. (For a historical overview, see <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_psychiatry" title="Timeline of psychiatry">Timeline of psychiatry</a>.)
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Theory_and_focus">Theory and focus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Psychiatry&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Theory and focus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="quotebox pullquote floatright" style="width:24em;&#32;;"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r887775652">.mw-parser-output .quotebox{background-color:#F9F9F9;border:1px solid #aaa;box-sizing:border-box;padding:10px;font-size:88%;max-width:100%}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft{margin:0.5em 1.4em 0.8em 0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright{margin:0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.centered{margin:0.5em auto 0.8em auto}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft p,.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright p{font-style:inherit}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-title{background-color:#F9F9F9;text-align:center;font-size:larger;font-weight:bold}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:before{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" “ ";vertical-align:-45%;line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:after{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" ” ";line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .left-aligned{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .right-aligned{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .center-aligned{text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .quotebox cite{display:block;font-style:normal}@media screen and (max-width:360px){.mw-parser-output .quotebox{min-width:100%;margin:0 0 0.8em!important;float:none!important}}</style>
<div class="quotebox-quote left-aligned" style="">"Psychiatry, more than any other branch of medicine, forces its practitioners to wrestle with the nature of evidence, the validity of introspection, problems in communication, and other long-standing philosophical issues" <small>(<a href="/wiki/Psychiatry#cite_note-Guze4-5" title="Psychiatry">Guze, 1992, p.4</a>).</small></div>
</div>
<p>Psychiatry is the field of medicine focused specifically on the <a href="/wiki/Mind" title="Mind">mind</a>, aiming to <a href="/wiki/Medical_research" title="Medical research">study</a>, <a href="/wiki/Preventive_healthcare" title="Preventive healthcare">prevent</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Treatment_of_mental_disorders" title="Treatment of mental disorders">treat</a> <a href="/wiki/Mental_disorder" title="Mental disorder">mental disorders</a> in <a href="/wiki/Human" title="Human">humans</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Guze4_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guze4-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Storrow1_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Storrow1-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELyness19973_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELyness19973-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> It has been described as an intermediary between the world from a social context and the world from the perspective of those who are mentally ill.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGask20047_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGask20047-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>People who specialize in psychiatry often differ from most other <a href="/wiki/Mental_health_professional" title="Mental health professional">mental health professionals</a> and <a href="/wiki/Physician" title="Physician">physicians</a> in that they must be familiar with both the <a href="/wiki/Social_science" title="Social science">social</a> and <a href="/wiki/Biology" title="Biology">biological sciences</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Storrow1_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Storrow1-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> The discipline studies the operations of different organs and body systems as classified by the patient's subjective experiences and the objective physiology of the patient. <sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuze1992131_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuze1992131-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Psychiatry treats mental disorders, which are conventionally divided into three very general categories: <a href="/wiki/Mental_disorder" title="Mental disorder">mental illnesses</a>, severe learning disabilities, and <a href="/wiki/Personality_disorder" title="Personality disorder">personality disorders</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGask2004113_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGask2004113-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> While the focus of psychiatry has changed little over time, the diagnostic and treatment processes have evolved dramatically and continue to do so. Since the late 20th century the field of psychiatry has continued to become more biological and less conceptually isolated from other medical fields.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGask2004128_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGask2004128-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Scope_of_practice">Scope of practice</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Psychiatry&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Scope of practice">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Neurology#Overlap_with_psychiatry" title="Neurology">Neurology §&#160;Overlap with psychiatry</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Neuropsychiatric_conditions_world_map_-_DALY_-_WHO2002.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Neuropsychiatric_conditions_world_map_-_DALY_-_WHO2002.svg/250px-Neuropsychiatric_conditions_world_map_-_DALY_-_WHO2002.svg.png" decoding="async" width="250" height="110" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Neuropsychiatric_conditions_world_map_-_DALY_-_WHO2002.svg/375px-Neuropsychiatric_conditions_world_map_-_DALY_-_WHO2002.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Neuropsychiatric_conditions_world_map_-_DALY_-_WHO2002.svg/500px-Neuropsychiatric_conditions_world_map_-_DALY_-_WHO2002.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="940" data-file-height="415" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Neuropsychiatric_conditions_world_map_-_DALY_-_WHO2002.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Disability-adjusted_life_year" title="Disability-adjusted life year">Disability-adjusted life year</a> for neuropsychiatric conditions per 100,000&#160;inhabitants in 2002.<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r886047268">.mw-parser-output .refbegin{font-size:90%;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .refbegin-hanging-indents>ul{list-style-type:none;margin-left:0}.mw-parser-output .refbegin-hanging-indents>ul>li,.mw-parser-output .refbegin-hanging-indents>dl>dd{margin-left:0;padding-left:3.2em;text-indent:-3.2em;list-style:none}.mw-parser-output .refbegin-100{font-size:100%}</style><div class="refbegin columns references-column-count references-column-count-2" style="-moz-column-count: 2; -webkit-column-count: 2; column-count: 2;"> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #b3b3b3; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;no data</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #ffff65; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;less than 10</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #fff200; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;10-20</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #ffdc00; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;20-30</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #ffc600; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;30-40</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #ffb000; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;40-50</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #ff9a00; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;50-60</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #ff8400; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;60-80</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #ff6e00; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;80-100</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #ff5800; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;100-120</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #ff4200; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;120-140</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #ff2c00; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;140-150</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #cb0000; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;more than 150</div></div></div></div></div>
<p>Though the medical specialty of psychiatry uses research in the field of <a href="/wiki/Neuroscience" title="Neuroscience">neuroscience</a>, <a href="/wiki/Psychology" title="Psychology">psychology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Medicine" title="Medicine">medicine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Biology" title="Biology">biology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Biochemistry" title="Biochemistry">biochemistry</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Pharmacology" title="Pharmacology">pharmacology</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Pietrini_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pietrini-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> it has generally been considered a middle ground between <a href="/wiki/Neurology" title="Neurology">neurology</a> and psychology.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShorter1997326_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShorter1997326-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> Because psychiatry and neurology are deeply intertwined medical specialties, all certification for both specialties and for their subspecialties is offered by a single board, the American Board of Psychiatry and Neurology, one of the member boards of the American Board of Medical Specialties.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> Unlike other physicians and neurologists, psychiatrists specialize in the <a href="/wiki/Doctor%E2%80%93patient_relationship" title="Doctor–patient relationship">doctor–patient relationship</a> and are trained to varying extents in the use of psychotherapy and other therapeutic communication techniques.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShorter1997326_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShorter1997326-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> Psychiatrists also differ from psychologists in that they are physicians and have post-graduate training called residency (usually 4 to 5 years) in psychiatry; the quality and thoroughness of their graduate medical training is identical to that of all other physicians.<sup id="cite_ref-Hauser_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hauser-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> Psychiatrists can therefore counsel patients, prescribe medication, order <a href="/wiki/Medical_laboratory" title="Medical laboratory">laboratory tests</a>, order <a href="/wiki/Neuroimaging" title="Neuroimaging">neuroimaging</a>, and conduct <a href="/wiki/Physical_examination" title="Physical examination">physical examinations</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-NIMHSite_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NIMHSite-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethics">Ethics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Psychiatry&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Ethics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Ethical_issues_in_psychiatry_(disambiguation)" class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" title="Ethical issues in psychiatry (disambiguation)">Ethical issues in psychiatry (disambiguation)</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/World_Psychiatric_Association" title="World Psychiatric Association">World Psychiatric Association</a> issues an <a href="/wiki/Ethical_code" title="Ethical code">ethical code</a> to govern the conduct of psychiatrists (like other purveyors of <a href="/wiki/Professional_ethics" title="Professional ethics">professional ethics</a>). The psychiatric code of ethics, first set forth through the Declaration of Hawaii in 1977 has been expanded through a 1983 Vienna update and in the broader Madrid Declaration in 1996. The code was further revised during the organization's general assemblies in 1999, 2002, 2005, and 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-WPAethics_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WPAethics-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The World Psychiatric Association code covers such matters as:  <a href="/wiki/Confidentiality" title="Confidentiality">confidentiality</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Capital_punishment" title="Capital punishment">death penalty</a>, ethnic or cultural discrimination,<sup id="cite_ref-WPAethics_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WPAethics-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>  <a href="/wiki/Euthanasia" title="Euthanasia">euthanasia</a>, genetics,  the <a href="/wiki/Dignity" title="Dignity">human dignity</a> of incapacitated patients, media relations,  organ transplantation, patient assessment, research ethics, sex selection,<sup id="cite_ref-Lopez_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lopez-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Torture" title="Torture">torture</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Gluzman_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gluzman-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Debreu_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Debreu-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>  and up-to-date knowledge. The ethical aspects described are increasingly being incorporated into the specialist curricula and psychiatric training.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In establishing such ethical codes, the profession has responded to a number of controversies about the practice of psychiatry, for example, surrounding the use of <a href="/wiki/Lobotomy" title="Lobotomy">lobotomy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Electroconvulsive_therapy" title="Electroconvulsive therapy">electroconvulsive therapy</a>.
</p><p>Discredited psychiatrists who operated outside the norms of <a href="/wiki/Medical_ethics" title="Medical ethics">medical ethics</a> include <a href="/wiki/Harry_Bailey" title="Harry Bailey">Harry Bailey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Donald_Ewen_Cameron" title="Donald Ewen Cameron">Donald Ewen Cameron</a>, <a href="/wiki/Samuel_A._Cartwright" title="Samuel A. Cartwright">Samuel A. Cartwright</a>, <a href="/wiki/Henry_Cotton_(doctor)" title="Henry Cotton (doctor)">Henry Cotton</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Andrei_Snezhnevsky" title="Andrei Snezhnevsky">Andrei Snezhnevsky</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Kirk2013_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kirk2013-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (March 2015)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Approaches">Approaches</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Psychiatry&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Approaches">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Psychiatric illnesses can be conceptualised in a number of different ways. The <a href="/wiki/Biomedical_model" title="Biomedical model">biomedical</a> approach examines signs and symptoms and compares them with diagnostic criteria. Mental illness can be assessed, conversely, through a narrative which tries to incorporate symptoms into a meaningful life history and to frame them as responses to external conditions. Both approaches are important in the field of psychiatry,<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> but have not sufficiently reconciled to settle <a href="/wiki/Biopsychiatry_controversy" title="Biopsychiatry controversy">controversy</a> over either the selection of a psychiatric <a href="/wiki/Paradigm" title="Paradigm">paradigm</a> or the specification of <a href="/wiki/Psychopathology" title="Psychopathology">psychopathology</a>. The notion of a "<a href="/wiki/Biopsychosocial_model" title="Biopsychosocial model">biopsychosocial model</a>" is often used to underline the multifactorial nature of clinical impairment.<sup id="cite_ref-McLaren_N_1998_86–92;_discussion_93–6_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McLaren_N_1998_86–92;_discussion_93–6-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-McLaren_madness_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McLaren_madness-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-McLaren_psychiatry_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McLaren_psychiatry-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> In this notion the word "model" is not used in a strictly scientific way though.<sup id="cite_ref-McLaren_N_1998_86–92;_discussion_93–6_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McLaren_N_1998_86–92;_discussion_93–6-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> Alternatively, a <a href="/w/index.php?title=Niall_McLaren&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Niall McLaren (page does not exist)">"biocognitive model"</a> acknowledges the physiological basis for the mind's existence, but identifies <a href="/wiki/Cognition" title="Cognition">cognition</a> as an <a href="/wiki/Antireductionism" title="Antireductionism">irreducible</a> and independent realm in which disorder may occur.<sup id="cite_ref-McLaren_N_1998_86–92;_discussion_93–6_26-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McLaren_N_1998_86–92;_discussion_93–6-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-McLaren_madness_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McLaren_madness-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-McLaren_psychiatry_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McLaren_psychiatry-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> The biocognitive approach includes a <a href="/wiki/Mentalism_(philosophy)" title="Mentalism (philosophy)">mentalist</a> <a href="/wiki/Etiology" title="Etiology">etiology</a> and provides a natural <a href="/wiki/Dualism_(philosophy_of_mind)" class="mw-redirect" title="Dualism (philosophy of mind)">dualist</a> (i.e. non-spiritual) revision of the biopsychosocial view, reflecting the efforts of <a href="/wiki/Australians" title="Australians">Australian</a> psychiatrist <a href="/w/index.php?title=Niall_McLaren&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Niall McLaren (page does not exist)">Niall McLaren</a> to bring the discipline into scientific maturity in accordance with the paradigmatic standards of <a href="/wiki/Philosophy_of_science" title="Philosophy of science">philosopher</a> <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Kuhn" title="Thomas Kuhn">Thomas Kuhn</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-McLaren_N_1998_86–92;_discussion_93–6_26-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McLaren_N_1998_86–92;_discussion_93–6-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-McLaren_madness_27-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McLaren_madness-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-McLaren_psychiatry_28-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McLaren_psychiatry-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Once a medical professional diagnoses a patient there are numerous ways that they could choose to treat the patient. Often psychiatrists will develop a treatment strategy that incorporates different facets of different approaches into one. Drug prescriptions are very commonly written to be regimented to patients along with any therapy they receive. There are three major pillars of psychotherapy that treatment strategies are most regularly drawn from. <a href="/wiki/Humanistic_psychology" title="Humanistic psychology">Humanistic psychology</a> attempts to put the "whole" of the patient in perspective; it also focuses on self exploration.<sup id="cite_ref-humanistic_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-humanistic-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Behaviorism" title="Behaviorism">Behaviorism</a> is a therapeutic school of thought that elects to focus solely on real and observable events, rather than mining the unconscious or <i>subconscious</i>. <a href="/wiki/Psychoanalysis" title="Psychoanalysis">Psychoanalysis</a>, on the other hand, concentrates its dealings on early childhood, irrational drives, the unconscious, and conflict between conscious and unconscious streams.<sup id="cite_ref-psychoanalysis_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-psychoanalysis-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Practitioners">Practitioners</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Psychiatry&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Practitioners">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Psychiatrist" title="Psychiatrist">Psychiatrist</a></div>
<table class="box-One_source plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-one_source" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><img alt="Question book-new.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>relies largely or entirely upon a <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Identifying_reliable_sources" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:Identifying reliable sources">single source</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Relevant discussion may be found on the <a href="/wiki/Talk:Psychiatry##" title="Talk:Psychiatry">talk page</a>. Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Psychiatry&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by introducing <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">citations</a> to additional sources.</span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">August 2017</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>All <a href="/wiki/Physician" title="Physician">physicians</a> can diagnose mental disorders and prescribe treatments utilizing principles of psychiatry. <a href="/wiki/Psychiatrist" title="Psychiatrist">Psychiatrists</a> are trained physicians who specialize in psychiatry and are certified to treat <a href="/wiki/Mental_illness" class="mw-redirect" title="Mental illness">mental illness</a>. They may treat outpatients, inpatients, or both; they may practice as solo practitioners or as members of groups; they may be self-employed, be members of partnerships, or be employees of governmental, academic, nonprofit, or for-profit entities; employees of hospitals; they may treat military personnel as civilians or as members of the military; and in any of these settings they may function as clinicians, researchers, teachers, or some combination of these. Although psychiatrists may also go through significant training to conduct <a href="/wiki/Psychotherapy" title="Psychotherapy">psychotherapy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Psychoanalysis" title="Psychoanalysis">psychoanalysis</a> or <a href="/wiki/Cognitive_behavioral_therapy" title="Cognitive behavioral therapy">cognitive behavioral therapy</a>, it is their training as physicians that differentiates them from other <a href="/wiki/Mental_health_professional" title="Mental health professional">mental health professionals</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="As_a_career_choice">As a career choice</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Psychiatry&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: As a career choice">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Psychiatry was not a popular career choice among medical students, even though medical school placements are rated favorably.<sup id="cite_ref-link.springer.com_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-link.springer.com-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> This has resulted in a significant shortage of psychiatrists in the United States and elsewhere.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> Strategies to address this shortfall have included the use of short 'taster' placements early in the medical school curriculum <sup id="cite_ref-link.springer.com_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-link.springer.com-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> and attempts to extend psychiatry services further using <a href="/wiki/Telemedicine" class="mw-redirect" title="Telemedicine">telemedicine</a> technologies and other methods.<sup id="cite_ref-THIELE_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-THIELE-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> As of 2015, however, there has been an increase in the number of medical students entering into a psychiatry residency. There are several reasons for this surge including the interesting nature of the field, growing interest in genetic biomarkers involved in psychiatric diagnoses, and newer pharmaceuticals on the drug market to treat psychiatric illnesses.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Subspecialties">Subspecialties</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Psychiatry&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Subspecialties">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The field of psychiatry has many subspecialties that require additional training and certification by the <a href="/wiki/American_Board_of_Psychiatry_and_Neurology" title="American Board of Psychiatry and Neurology">American Board of Psychiatry and Neurology</a> (ABPN). Such subspecialties include:<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Addiction_psychiatry" title="Addiction psychiatry">Addiction psychiatry</a></li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brain_Injury_Medicine&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Brain Injury Medicine (page does not exist)">Brain Injury Medicine</a><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Child_and_Adolescent_Psychiatry" class="mw-redirect" title="Child and Adolescent Psychiatry">Child and Adolescent Psychiatry</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Clinical_neurophysiology" title="Clinical neurophysiology">Clinical neurophysiology</a></li>
<li>Epilepsy<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Forensic_psychiatry" title="Forensic psychiatry">Forensic psychiatry</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Geriatric_psychiatry" title="Geriatric psychiatry">Geriatric psychiatry</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hospice_and_palliative_medicine" title="Hospice and palliative medicine">Hospice and palliative medicine</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Pain_medicine" class="mw-redirect" title="Pain medicine">Pain medicine</a><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Psychosomatic_medicine" title="Psychosomatic medicine">Psychosomatic medicine</a><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> (also known as <a href="/wiki/Liaison_psychiatry" title="Liaison psychiatry">consultation-liaison psychiatry</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sleep_medicine" title="Sleep medicine">Sleep medicine</a><sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<p>Additional psychiatry subspecialties, for which <a href="/wiki/American_Board_of_Psychiatry_and_Neurology" title="American Board of Psychiatry and Neurology">ABPN</a> does not offer certification, include:<sup id="cite_ref-UKReq_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UKReq-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Cross-cultural_psychiatry" title="Cross-cultural psychiatry">Cross-cultural psychiatry</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Emergency_psychiatry" title="Emergency psychiatry">Emergency psychiatry</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Learning_disability" title="Learning disability">Learning disability</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Neurodevelopmental_disorder" title="Neurodevelopmental disorder">Neurodevelopmental disorder</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cognition" title="Cognition">Cognition</a> diseases as in various forms of <a href="/wiki/Dementia" title="Dementia">dementia</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Biological_psychiatry" title="Biological psychiatry">Biological psychiatry</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Community_psychiatry" class="mw-redirect" title="Community psychiatry">Community psychiatry</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Global_Mental_Health" class="mw-redirect" title="Global Mental Health">Global Mental Health</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Military_psychiatry" title="Military psychiatry">Military psychiatry</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Social_psychiatry" title="Social psychiatry">Social psychiatry</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Neuropsychiatry" title="Neuropsychiatry">Neuropsychiatry</a></li></ul>
<p><a href="/wiki/Addiction_psychiatry" title="Addiction psychiatry">Addiction psychiatry</a> focuses on evaluation and treatment of individuals with alcohol, drug, or other substance-related disorders, and of individuals with dual diagnosis of substance-related and other psychiatric disorders. <a href="/wiki/Biological_psychiatry" title="Biological psychiatry">Biological psychiatry</a> is an approach to psychiatry that aims to understand mental disorders in terms of the biological function of the nervous system. <a href="/wiki/Child_and_adolescent_psychiatry" title="Child and adolescent psychiatry">Child and adolescent psychiatry</a> is the branch of psychiatry that specializes in work with children, teenagers, and their families. <a href="/wiki/Community_psychiatry" class="mw-redirect" title="Community psychiatry">Community psychiatry</a> is an approach that reflects an inclusive <a href="/wiki/Public_health" title="Public health">public health</a> perspective and is practiced in <a href="/wiki/Community_mental_health_services" class="mw-redirect" title="Community mental health services">community mental health services</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Cross-cultural_psychiatry" title="Cross-cultural psychiatry">Cross-cultural psychiatry</a> is a branch of psychiatry concerned with the cultural and ethnic context of mental disorder and psychiatric services. <a href="/wiki/Emergency_psychiatry" title="Emergency psychiatry">Emergency psychiatry</a> is the clinical application of psychiatry in emergency settings. <a href="/wiki/Forensic_psychiatry" title="Forensic psychiatry">Forensic psychiatry</a> utilizes medical science generally, and psychiatric knowledge and assessment methods in particular, to help answer legal questions. <a href="/wiki/Geriatric_psychiatry" title="Geriatric psychiatry">Geriatric psychiatry</a> is a branch of psychiatry dealing with the study, prevention, and treatment of mental disorders in the <a href="/wiki/Old_age" title="Old age">elderly</a>. <a href="/wiki/Global_Mental_Health" class="mw-redirect" title="Global Mental Health">Global Mental Health</a> is an area of study, research and practice that places a priority on improving mental health and achieving equity in mental health for all people worldwide,<sup id="cite_ref-Patel_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Patel-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> although some scholars consider it to be a neo-colonial, culturally insensitive project.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Liaison_psychiatry" title="Liaison psychiatry">Liaison psychiatry</a> is the branch of psychiatry that specializes in the interface between other medical specialties and psychiatry. <a href="/wiki/Military_psychiatry" title="Military psychiatry">Military psychiatry</a> covers special aspects of psychiatry and mental disorders within the military context. <a href="/wiki/Neuropsychiatry" title="Neuropsychiatry">Neuropsychiatry</a> is a branch of medicine dealing with mental disorders attributable to diseases of the nervous system. <a href="/wiki/Social_psychiatry" title="Social psychiatry">Social psychiatry</a> is a branch of psychiatry that focuses on the interpersonal and cultural context of mental disorder and mental well-being.
</p><p>In larger healthcare organizations, psychiatrists often serve in senior management roles, where they are responsible for the efficient and effective delivery of mental health services for the organization's constituents. For example, the Chief of Mental Health Services at most VA medical centers is usually a psychiatrist, although psychologists occasionally are selected for the position as well.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>In the United States, psychiatry is one of the few specialties which qualify for further education and board-certification in <a href="/wiki/Pain_management" title="Pain management">pain medicine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Palliative_care" title="Palliative care">palliative medicine</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sleep_medicine" title="Sleep medicine">sleep medicine</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Research">Research</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Psychiatry&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Research">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Psychiatric research is, by its very nature, interdisciplinary; combining social, biological and psychological perspectives in attempt to understand the nature and treatment of mental disorders.<sup id="cite_ref-UManchester_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UManchester-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> Clinical and research psychiatrists study basic and clinical psychiatric topics at research institutions and publish articles in journals.<sup id="cite_ref-Pietrini_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pietrini-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NYSPI_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYSPI-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CPRF_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CPRF-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Elsevier_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Elsevier-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> Under the supervision of <a href="/wiki/Institutional_review_board" title="Institutional review board">institutional review boards</a>, psychiatric clinical researchers look at topics such as neuroimaging, genetics, and psychopharmacology in order to enhance diagnostic validity and reliability, to discover new treatment methods, and to classify new mental disorders.<sup id="cite_ref-Mitchell_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mitchell-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (August 2017)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> <sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Clinical_application">Clinical application</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Psychiatry&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Clinical application">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Diagnostic_systems">Diagnostic systems</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Psychiatry&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Diagnostic systems">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Diagnostic_classification_and_rating_scales_used_in_psychiatry" class="mw-redirect" title="Diagnostic classification and rating scales used in psychiatry">Diagnostic classification and rating scales used in psychiatry</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Psychiatric_assessment" title="Psychiatric assessment">Psychiatric diagnoses</a> take place in a wide variety of settings and are performed by many different <a href="/wiki/Health_care_provider" class="mw-redirect" title="Health care provider">health professionals</a>. Therefore, the diagnostic procedure may vary greatly based upon these factors. Typically, though, a psychiatric diagnosis utilizes a <a href="/wiki/Differential_diagnosis" title="Differential diagnosis">differential diagnosis</a> procedure where a <a href="/wiki/Mental_status_examination" title="Mental status examination">mental status examination</a> and physical examination is conducted, with <a href="/wiki/Pathological" class="mw-redirect" title="Pathological">pathological</a>, <a href="/wiki/Psychopathological" class="mw-redirect" title="Psychopathological">psychopathological</a> or <a href="/wiki/Psychosocial" title="Psychosocial">psychosocial</a> histories obtained, and sometimes <a href="/wiki/Neuroimaging" title="Neuroimaging">neuroimages</a> or other <a href="/wiki/Neurophysiological" class="mw-redirect" title="Neurophysiological">neurophysiological</a> measurements are taken, or <a href="/wiki/Personality_test" title="Personality test">personality tests</a> or <a href="/wiki/Cognitive_test" title="Cognitive test">cognitive tests</a> administered.<sup id="cite_ref-Meyendorf_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Meyendorf-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELyness199710_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELyness199710-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Hampel_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hampel-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Townsend_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Townsend-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> In some cases, a brain scan might be used to rule out other medical illnesses, but at this time relying on brain scans alone cannot accurately diagnose a mental illness or tell the risk of getting a mental illness in the future.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> A few psychiatrists are beginning to utilize <a href="/wiki/Genetics" title="Genetics">genetics</a> during the diagnostic process but on the whole this remains a research topic.<sup id="cite_ref-Krebs_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Krebs-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Benes_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Benes-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Vonk_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vonk-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Diagnostic_manuals">Diagnostic manuals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Psychiatry&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Diagnostic manuals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Diagnostic_and_Statistical_Manual_of_Mental_Disorders" title="Diagnostic and Statistical Manual of Mental Disorders">Diagnostic and Statistical Manual of Mental Disorders</a></div>
<p>Three main diagnostic manuals used to classify mental health conditions are in use today. The <a href="/wiki/ICD-10" title="ICD-10">ICD-10</a> is produced and published by the <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a>, includes a section on psychiatric conditions, and is used worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-ICD10_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ICD10-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Diagnostic_and_Statistical_Manual_of_Mental_Disorders" title="Diagnostic and Statistical Manual of Mental Disorders">Diagnostic and Statistical Manual of Mental Disorders</a>, produced and published by the <a href="/wiki/American_Psychiatric_Association" title="American Psychiatric Association">American Psychiatric Association</a>, is primarily focused on mental health conditions and is the main classification tool in the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DSM_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DSM-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> It is currently in its fifth revised edition and is also used worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-DSM_66-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DSM-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Society_of_Psychiatry" title="Chinese Society of Psychiatry">Chinese Society of Psychiatry</a> has also produced a diagnostic manual, the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Classification_of_Mental_Disorders" title="Chinese Classification of Mental Disorders">Chinese Classification of Mental Disorders</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Chen_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chen-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The stated intention of diagnostic manuals is typically to develop replicable and clinically useful categories and criteria, to facilitate consensus and agreed upon standards, whilst being atheoretical as regards etiology.<sup id="cite_ref-DSM_66-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DSM-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Essen_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Essen-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> However, the categories are nevertheless based on particular psychiatric theories and data; they are broad and often specified by numerous possible combinations of symptoms, and many of the categories overlap in symptomology or typically occur together.<sup id="cite_ref-Mezzich_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mezzich-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> While originally intended only as a guide for experienced clinicians trained in its use, the nomenclature is now widely used by clinicians, administrators and insurance companies in many countries.<sup id="cite_ref-Guze2_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guze2-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The DSM has attracted praise for standardizing psychiatric diagnostic categories and criteria. It has also attracted controversy and criticism. Some critics argue that the DSM represents an <a href="/wiki/Unscientific" class="mw-redirect" title="Unscientific">unscientific</a> system that enshrines the opinions of a few powerful psychiatrists. There are ongoing issues concerning the <a href="/wiki/Validity_(statistics)" title="Validity (statistics)">validity</a> and <a href="/wiki/Reliability_(statistics)" title="Reliability (statistics)">reliability</a> of the diagnostic categories; the reliance on superficial <a href="/wiki/Symptoms" class="mw-redirect" title="Symptoms">symptoms</a>; the use of artificial dividing lines between categories and from '<a href="/wiki/Normality_(behavior)" title="Normality (behavior)">normality</a>'; possible <a href="/wiki/Cultural" class="mw-redirect" title="Cultural">cultural</a> bias; <a href="/wiki/Medicalization" title="Medicalization">medicalization</a> of human distress and financial <a href="/wiki/Conflicts_of_interest" class="mw-redirect" title="Conflicts of interest">conflicts of interest</a>, including with the practice of psychiatrists and with the <a href="/wiki/Pharmaceutical_industry" title="Pharmaceutical industry">pharmaceutical industry</a>; political controversies about the inclusion or exclusion of diagnoses from the manual, in general or in regard to specific issues; and the experience of those who are most directly affected by the manual by being diagnosed, including the <a href="/wiki/Consumer/survivor_movement" class="mw-redirect" title="Consumer/survivor movement">consumer/survivor movement</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-concept&amp;evolution_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-concept&amp;evolution-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> The publication of the DSM, with tightly guarded copyrights, now makes APA over $5 million a year, historically adding up to over $100 million.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Treatment">Treatment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Psychiatry&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Treatment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="box-Cleanup_rewrite plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Crystal_Clear_app_kedit.svg" class="image"><img alt="Crystal Clear app kedit.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Crystal_Clear_app_kedit.svg/40px-Crystal_Clear_app_kedit.svg.png" decoding="async" width="40" height="40" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Crystal_Clear_app_kedit.svg/60px-Crystal_Clear_app_kedit.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Crystal_Clear_app_kedit.svg/80px-Crystal_Clear_app_kedit.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="128" data-file-height="128" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section may need to be <b>rewritten</b> to comply with Wikipedia's <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style">quality standards</a>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Psychiatry&amp;action=edit">You can help</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Talk:Psychiatry" title="Talk:Psychiatry">discussion page</a> may contain suggestions.</span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">May 2009</span>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="General_considerations">General considerations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Psychiatry&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: General considerations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:NIMH_Clinical_Center.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/NIMH_Clinical_Center.JPG/220px-NIMH_Clinical_Center.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/NIMH_Clinical_Center.JPG/330px-NIMH_Clinical_Center.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/NIMH_Clinical_Center.JPG/440px-NIMH_Clinical_Center.JPG 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:NIMH_Clinical_Center.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>NIMH federal agency patient room for Psychiatric research, Maryland, USA.</div></div></div>
<p>Individuals with mental health conditions are commonly referred to as <i><a href="/wiki/Patient" title="Patient">patients</a></i> but may also be called <i><a href="/wiki/Customer" title="Customer">clients</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Consumer" title="Consumer">consumers</a></i>, or <i>service recipients</i>. They may come under the care of a psychiatric physician or other psychiatric practitioners by various paths, the two most common being self-<a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/referral" class="extiw" title="wikt:referral">referral</a> or referral by a <a href="/wiki/Primary_care_physician" title="Primary care physician">primary care physician</a>. Alternatively, a person may be referred by hospital medical staff, by <a href="/wiki/Court_order" title="Court order">court order</a>, <a href="/wiki/Involuntary_commitment" title="Involuntary commitment">involuntary commitment</a>, or, in the UK and Australia, by <a href="/wiki/Sectioning" class="mw-redirect" title="Sectioning">sectioning</a> under a <a href="/wiki/Mental_health_law" title="Mental health law">mental health law</a>.
</p><p>Persons who undergo a <a href="/wiki/Psychiatric_assessment" title="Psychiatric assessment">psychiatric assessment</a> are evaluated by a <a href="/wiki/Psychiatrist" title="Psychiatrist">psychiatrist</a> for their mental and physical condition. This usually involves interviewing the person and often obtaining information from other sources such as other health and social care professionals, relatives, associates, law enforcement personnel, emergency medical personnel, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_diagnostic_classification_and_rating_scales_used_in_psychiatry" title="List of diagnostic classification and rating scales used in psychiatry">psychiatric rating scales</a>. A <a href="/wiki/Mental_status_examination" title="Mental status examination">mental status examination</a> is carried out, and a <a href="/wiki/Physical_examination" title="Physical examination">physical examination</a> is usually performed to establish or exclude other illnesses that may be contributing to the alleged psychiatric problems. A physical examination may also serve to identify any signs of <a href="/wiki/Self-harm" title="Self-harm">self-harm</a>; this examination is often performed by someone other than the psychiatrist, especially if <a href="/wiki/Blood_test" title="Blood test">blood tests</a> and <a href="/wiki/Medical_imaging" title="Medical imaging">medical imaging</a> are performed.
</p><p>Like most medications, psychiatric medications can cause <a href="/wiki/Adverse_effect_(medicine)" class="mw-redirect" title="Adverse effect (medicine)">adverse effects</a> in patients, and some require ongoing <a href="/wiki/Therapeutic_drug_monitoring" title="Therapeutic drug monitoring">therapeutic drug monitoring</a>, for instance <a href="/wiki/Full_blood_count" class="mw-redirect" title="Full blood count">full blood counts</a> <a href="/wiki/Blood_plasma" title="Blood plasma">serum</a> drug levels, renal function, liver function or thyroid function. <a href="/wiki/Electroconvulsive_therapy" title="Electroconvulsive therapy">Electroconvulsive therapy</a> (ECT) is sometimes administered for serious and disabling conditions, such as those unresponsive to medication. The efficacy<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> and adverse effects of psychiatric drugs may vary from patient to patient.
</p><p>For many years, controversy has surrounded the use of involuntary treatment and use of the term "lack of insight" in describing patients. Mental health laws vary significantly among jurisdictions, but in many cases, involuntary psychiatric treatment is permitted when there is deemed to be a risk to the patient or others due to the patient's illness. Involuntary treatment refers to treatment that occurs based on the treating physician's recommendations without requiring consent from the patient.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Mental health issues such as mood disorders and schizophrenia and other psychotic disorders were the most common principle diagnoses for Medicaid super-utilizers in the United States in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Inpatient_treatment">Inpatient treatment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Psychiatry&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Inpatient treatment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="box-More_citations_needed_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Psychiatry&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.<br /><small><span class="plainlinks"><i>Find sources:</i>&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?as_eq=wikipedia&amp;q=%22Psychiatry%22">"Psychiatry"</a>&#160;–&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbm=nws&amp;q=%22Psychiatry%22+-wikipedia">news</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?&amp;q=%22Psychiatry%22+site:news.google.com/newspapers&amp;source=newspapers">newspapers</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbs=bks:1&amp;q=%22Psychiatry%22+-wikipedia">books</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//scholar.google.com/scholar?q=%22Psychiatry%22">scholar</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.jstor.org/action/doBasicSearch?Query=%22Psychiatry%22&amp;acc=on&amp;wc=on">JSTOR</a></span></small></span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">August 2017</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><a href="/wiki/Treatment_of_mental_illness" class="mw-redirect" title="Treatment of mental illness">Psychiatric treatments</a> have changed over the past several decades. In the past, psychiatric patients were often <a href="/wiki/Psychiatric_hospital" title="Psychiatric hospital">hospitalized</a> for six months or more, with some cases involving hospitalization for many years. Today in most countries, people receiving psychiatric treatment are more likely to be seen as <a href="/wiki/General_out-patient_clinic" class="mw-redirect" title="General out-patient clinic">outpatients</a>. Average inpatient psychiatric  treatment stay has decreased significantly since the 1960s, a trend known as <a href="/wiki/Deinstitutionalization" class="mw-redirect" title="Deinstitutionalization">deinstitutionalization</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> However, in Japan psychiatric hospitals continue to keep patients for long periods, sometimes even keeping them in <a href="/wiki/Physical_restraints" class="mw-redirect" title="Physical restraints">physical restraints</a>, strapped to their beds for periods of weeks or months.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Psychiatric inpatients are people admitted to a hospital or clinic to receive psychiatric care. Some are admitted involuntarily, perhaps committed to a secure hospital, or in some jurisdictions to a facility within the prison system. In many countries including the US and Canada, the criteria for involuntary admission vary with local jurisdiction. They may be as broad as having a mental health condition, or as narrow as being an immediate danger to themselves or others. Bed availability is often the real determinant of admission decisions to hard pressed public facilities. European Human Rights legislation restricts detention to medically certified cases of mental disorder, and adds a right to timely judicial review of detention.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>People may be admitted voluntarily if the treating doctor considers that safety isn't compromised by this less restrictive option. Inpatient psychiatric wards may be secure (for those thought to have a particular risk of violence or self-harm) or unlocked/open. Some wards are mixed-sex whilst same-sex wards are increasingly favored to protect women inpatients. Once in the care of a hospital, people are <a href="/wiki/Psychiatric_assessment" title="Psychiatric assessment">assessed</a>, monitored, and often given medication and care from a multidisciplinary team, which may include physicians, pharmacists, psychiatric nurse practitioners, <a href="/wiki/Psychiatric_and_mental_health_nursing" title="Psychiatric and mental health nursing">psychiatric nurses</a>, clinical psychologists, psychotherapists, psychiatric social workers, occupational therapists and social workers. If a person receiving treatment in a psychiatric hospital is assessed as at particular risk of harming themselves or others, they may be put on constant or intermittent one-to-one supervision, and may be put in <a href="/wiki/Physical_restraints" class="mw-redirect" title="Physical restraints">physical restraints</a> or medicated. People on inpatient wards may be allowed leave for periods of time, either accompanied or on their own.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In many developed countries there has been a massive reduction in psychiatric beds since the mid 20th century, with the growth of community care. Standards of inpatient care remain a challenge in some public and private facilities, due to levels of funding, and facilities in developing countries are typically grossly inadequate for the same reason. Even in developed countries, programs in public hospitals vary widely. Some may offer structured activities and therapies offered from many perspectives while others may only have the funding for medicating and monitoring patients. This may be problematic in that the maximum amount of therapeutic work might not actually take place in the hospital setting. This is why hospitals are increasingly used in limited situations and moments of crisis where patients are a direct threat to themselves or others. Alternatives to psychiatric hospitals that may actively offer more therapeutic approaches include rehabilitation centers or "rehab" as popularly termed.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Outpatient_treatment">Outpatient treatment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Psychiatry&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Outpatient treatment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Outpatient treatment involves periodic visits to a psychiatrist for consultation in his or her office, or at a community-based outpatient clinic. Initial appointments, at which the psychiatrist conducts a psychiatric assessment or evaluation of the patient, are typically 45 to 75 minutes in length. Follow-up appointments are generally shorter in duration, i.e., 15 to 30 minutes, with a focus on making medication adjustments, reviewing potential medication interactions, considering the impact of other medical disorders on the patient's mental and emotional functioning, and counseling patients regarding changes they might make to facilitate healing and remission of symptoms (e.g., exercise, cognitive therapy techniques, sleep hygiene—to name just a few). The frequency with which a psychiatrist sees people in treatment varies widely, from once a week to twice a year, depending on the type, severity and stability of each person's condition, and depending on what the clinician and patient decide would be best.
</p><p>Increasingly, psychiatrists are limiting their practices to psychopharmacology (prescribing medications), as opposed to previous practice in which a psychiatrist would provide traditional 50-minute psychotherapy sessions, of which psychopharmacology would be a part, but most of the consultation sessions consisted of "talk therapy." This shift began in the early 1980s and accelerated in the 1990s and 2000s.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> A major reason for this change was the advent of managed care insurance plans, which began to limit reimbursement for psychotherapy sessions provided by psychiatrists. The underlying assumption was that psychopharmacology was at least as effective as psychotherapy, and it could be delivered more efficiently because less time is required for the appointment.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-pmid20048220_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pmid20048220-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-pmid11779262_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pmid11779262-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> For example, most psychiatrists schedule three or four follow-up appointments per hour, as opposed to seeing one patient per hour in the traditional psychotherapy model. Because of this shift in practice patterns, psychiatrists often refer patients whom they think would benefit from psychotherapy to other mental health professionals, e.g., clinical social workers and psychologists.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Psychiatry&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_psychiatry" title="History of psychiatry">History of psychiatry</a></div>
<p>The earliest known texts on mental disorders are from ancient India and include the Ayurvedic text, <a href="/wiki/Charaka_Samhita" title="Charaka Samhita">Charaka Samhita</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> The first hospitals for curing mental illness were established in India during the 3rd century BCE.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Greeks also created early manuscripts about mental disorders.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShorter19971_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShorter19971-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> In the 4th century BCE, <a href="/wiki/Hippocrates" title="Hippocrates">Hippocrates</a> theorized that physiological abnormalities may be the root of mental disorders.<sup id="cite_ref-Elkes13_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Elkes13-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> In 4th to 5th Century B.C. Greece, <a href="/wiki/Hippocrates" title="Hippocrates">Hippocrates</a> wrote that he visited <a href="/wiki/Democritus" title="Democritus">Democritus</a> and found him in his garden cutting open animals. Democritus explained that he was attempting to discover the cause of madness and melancholy. Hippocrates praised his work.
